</div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="2">\n         Description\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Role:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Supply the\n         <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n          International Space Station\n         </a>\n         with propellant, water, air, payload and experiments.\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Crew:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         None, but\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human-rated" title="Human-rated">\n          human-rated\n         </a>\n         .\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-1">\n           [1]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="2">\n         Dimensions\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Height:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         10.3\xc2\xa0m (34\xc2\xa0ft)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Diameter:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         4.5\xc2\xa0m (15\xc2\xa0ft)\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Con_2-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Con-2">\n           [2]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Launch Payload:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         7,667\xc2\xa0kg (16,903\xc2\xa0lb)\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esaspecs_3-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-esaspecs-3">\n           [3]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Return Payload:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         None\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Mass at launch:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         20,750\xc2\xa0kg\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Con_2-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-Con-2">\n           [2]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Pressurized Volume:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         48\xc2\xa0m\n         <sup>\n          3\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n          <a href="#cite_note-4">\n           [4]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="2">\n         Electrical Energy\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Source:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         4 solar panel wings of 4 panels each and 40Ah rechargeable batteries\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Size:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         total span 22.3 m\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Generated Power:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         3,800 W\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="2">\n         On-board engines\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Main engine:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         4 \xc3\x97 490N, Aerojet (GenCorp) Model\n         <a href="/wiki/R-4D" title="R-4D">\n          R-4D-11\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Thrusters\xc2\xa0:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         28 \xc3\x97 220N for\n         <a href="/wiki/Attitude_control" title="Attitude control">\n          attitude control\n         </a>\n         &amp; braking,\n         <a href="/wiki/ArianeGroup" title="ArianeGroup">\n          ArianeGroup\n         </a>\n         Lampoldshausen\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="2">\n         Performance\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Endurance:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Docked with the ISS for six months\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Apogee:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         400\xc2\xa0km\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Perigee:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         300\xc2\xa0km\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Inclination:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         51.6 degrees\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="2">\n         Launch\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Location:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/CNES" title="CNES">\n          CNES\n         </a>\n         \'s\n         <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Space_Centre" title="Guiana Space Centre">\n          Guiana Space Centre\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <br/>\n         <a href="/wiki/Kourou" title="Kourou">\n          Kourou\n         </a>\n         in French Guiana\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Site:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/ELA-3" title="ELA-3">\n          ELA-3\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          Booster:\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">\n          Ariane 5\n         </a>\n         ES\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        Automated Transfer Vehicle\n       </b>\n       , originally\n       <b>\n        Ariane Transfer Vehicle\n       </b>\n       or\n       <b>\n        ATV\n       </b>\n       , was an expendable\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automated_cargo_spacecraft" title="Automated cargo spacecraft">\n        cargo spacecraft\n       </a>\n       developed by the\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">\n        European Space Agency\n       </a>\n       (ESA).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It was operated in conjunction with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">\n        Ariane 5\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Heavy-lift_launch_vehicle" title="Heavy-lift launch vehicle">\n        heavy-lift launch vehicle\n       </a>\n       , which conveyed the ATV into orbit. It functions much like the Russian\n       <a href="/wiki/Progress_(spacecraft)" title="Progress (spacecraft)">\n        Progress cargo spacecraft\n       </a>\n       , but with three times the capacity.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A total of five ATVs,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Jules_Verne_ATV" title="Jules Verne ATV">\n         Jules Verne\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler_ATV" title="Johannes Kepler ATV">\n         Johannes Kepler\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Edoardo_Amaldi_ATV" title="Edoardo Amaldi ATV">\n         Edoardo Amaldi\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein_ATV" title="Albert Einstein ATV">\n         Albert Einstein\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Georges_Lema%C3%AEtre_ATV" title="Georges Lema\xc3\xaetre ATV">\n         Georges Lema\xc3\xaetre\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       were launched. Following several delays to the programme, the first of these was launched in March 2008. These ATVs performed supply missions to the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       (ISS), transporting various payloads such as propellant, water, air, food, and scientific research equipment; ATVs also\n       <a href="/wiki/Reboost" title="Reboost">\n        reboosted\n       </a>\n       the station into a higher\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">\n        orbit\n       </a>\n       while docked. It was an uncrewed platform that operated with a high level of automation, such as its docking sequence; at no point was it used for transporting passengers. On 2 April 2012, the ESA announced that the ATV program would be terminated following the launch of the fifth ATV in 2014.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spaceflightnow_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-spaceflightnow-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Further use of the ATV has been proposed. Various further developments, including crewed versions of the ATV as well as opportunities to reuse sections or elements of its technology, have been studied by both the ESA and\n       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Defence_and_Space" title="Airbus Defence and Space">\n        Airbus Defence and Space\n       </a>\n       , the principal manufacturer of the vehicle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atv_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-atv-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atv2_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-atv2-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2012, ESA member states decided that the ATV would be adapted to serve as the service module of the NASA\n       <a href="/wiki/Orion_(spacecraft)" title="Orion (spacecraft)">\n        Orion spacecraft\n       </a>\n       . In January 2013, the ESA and NASA announced that they were proceeding with a combined\n       <a href="/wiki/Orion_Service_Module" title="Orion Service Module">\n        Orion and ATV derived service module\n       </a>\n       , which would serve a major component for the in-development\n       <a href="/wiki/Orion_(spacecraft)" title="Orion (spacecraft)">\n        Orion crewed spacecraft\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-osm_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-osm-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a        </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Albert Einstein\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11">\n           <a class="toctext">\n           Exoliner\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Development">\n        Development\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Development">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">\n        Origins\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       During the 1990s, as the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station_program" title="International Space Station program">\n        International Space Station program\n       </a>\n       was taking place, it was collectively recognised by the 15 participating nations that, upon completion, the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       (ISS), a crewed\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">\n        space station\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n        Low Earth orbit\n       </a>\n       (LEO), would require regular resupply missions in order to meet the needs of the onboard crew as well as to deliver apparatus to support the various scientific tests that would be performed on board. In October 1995, it was agreed that, amongst the various contributions to the ISS program that Europe would assume responsibility for under the vestiges of the\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">\n        European Space Agency\n       </a>\n       (ESA), would be the\n       <i>\n        Automated Transfer Vehicle\n       </i>\n       , or ATV; this logistics-orientated spacecraft would perform the identified resupply missions to ISS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 9 December 1998, the ESA awarded a $470 million contract to proceed with development work on the ATV to French\n       <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">\n        aerospace\n       </a>\n       company\n       <a href="/wiki/A%C3%A9rospatiale" title="A\xc3\xa9rospatiale">\n        A\xc3\xa9rospatiale\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_contract_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_contract-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       While A\xc3\xa9rospatiale served as the principal contractor for the ATV, it was joined by multiple major subcontractors, including Italian manufacturer\n       <a href="/wiki/Thales_Alenia_Space" title="Thales Alenia Space">\n        Alenia Spazio\n       </a>\n       , Franco-British firm\n       <a href="/wiki/Matra_Marconi_Space" title="Matra Marconi Space">\n        Matra Marconi Space\n       </a>\n       and German aerospace company\n       <a href="/wiki/DASA" title="DASA">\n        DaimlerChrysler Aerospace\n       </a>\n       (DASA); some components were also provided by Russian firm\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S._P._Korolev_Rocket_and_Space_Corporation_Energia" title="S. P. Korolev Rocket and Space Corporation Energia">\n        S. P. Korolev Rocket and Space Corporation Energia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_contract_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_contract-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Prior to 2000, DASA was to serve as the prime contractor for production, after which the role would be gradually transferred to A\xc3\xa9rospatiale. At the point at which the contract had been awarded, it was envisioned that the first flight of the ATV would be conducted during September 2003.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_contract_13-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_contract-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atv_biway_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-atv_biway-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The launch of the first ATV, which had been named\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Jules_Verne_ATV" title="Jules Verne ATV">\n         Jules Verne\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , was subject to multiple delays, which were partially generated by problems encountered with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">\n        Ariane 5\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Heavy-lift_launch_vehicle" title="Heavy-lift launch vehicle">\n        heavy-lift launch vehicle\n       </a>\n       , as well as a substantial software re-write.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2007_delay_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2007_delay-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By May 2003, it was set to be launched sometime during late 2004.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003_save_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2003_save-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By mid 2004, it had been announced that launch of the first ATV, which was by then undergoing electrical testing following the completion of integration work, had been postponed due to technical issues, and was reportedly scheduled to be launched during late 2005, following the issuing of a renegotiated $1.1 billion contract between the ESA and the prime contractor.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atv_biway_14-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-atv_biway-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In March 2005, another launch delay was declared, due to the need for greater development of the failure-mode software along with launch-window timing changes, which put the planned ATV launch back from late 2005 to an undetermined date during 2006.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In October 2005, it was clarified that the new launch date for the first ATV would be during 2007.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2007_delay_17-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2007_delay-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In September 2006, it was announced that the final stage of testing on the Ariane 5\'s customised ATV stage was within its final phase.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In December 2006, it was announced that the first ATV had completed its\n       <a href="/wiki/Vacuum" title="Vacuum">\n        vacuum\n       </a>\n       test, marking the successful completion of the key tests and enabling a final launch date to be set.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In April 2007, the ATV was subject to four-month long qualification process in response to operational concerns, including safety queries originating from the U.S., and to examine the vehicle\'s potential commercialisation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2007_nasa_supply_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2007_nasa_supply-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Production">\n        Production\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Following multiple restructuring and ownership changes,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2003_save_18-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2003_save-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the prime contractor for the ATV became\n       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Defence_and_Space" title="Airbus Defence and Space">\n        Airbus Defence and Space\n       </a>\n       , whom lead a consortium of many sub-contractors. While development work have been started in\n       <a href="/wiki/Les_Mureaux" title="Les Mureaux">\n        Les Mureaux\n       </a>\n       , France, much of the activity relocated to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bremen_(city)" title="Bremen (city)">\n        Bremen\n       </a>\n       , Germany, as the project moved from its development to the production stage, in which work on the four initial units started. In order to facilitate the relationship between the contractor and the ESA, an integrated ESA team at the Les Mureaux site was established and maintained for the duration of the development.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Airbus Defence and Space builds the ATVs in its facility in Bremen. In 2004, contracts and accords were signed for four additional ATVs, which were envisioned to be launched at a rate of around one every two years, bringing the total order, including the first,\n       <i>\n        Jules-Verne\n       </i>\n       , to five vehicles. According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/German_Aerospace_Center" title="German Aerospace Center">\n        German Aerospace Center\n       </a>\n       (DLR), the development cost of the ATV was approximately \xe2\x82\xac1.35\xc2\xa0billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Reportedly, each ATV spacecraft was costed at roughly US$300\xc2\xa0million, which did not include launch costs.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In March 2005,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RSC_Energia" title="RSC Energia">\n        RSC Energia\n       </a>\n       signed a \xe2\x82\xac40\xc2\xa0million contract with one of the main subcontractors of Airbus Defence and Space, the Italian company\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alenia_Spazio" title="Alenia Spazio">\n        Alenia Spazio\n       </a>\n       (now\n       <a href="/wiki/Thales_Alenia_Space" title="Thales Alenia Space">\n        Thales Alenia Space\n       </a>\n       ), to supply the Russian Docking System, refuelling system, and Russian Equipment Control System.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSC-deal_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RSC-deal-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Within the Airbus Defence and Space led project, Thales Alenia Space is responsible for the pressurized cargo carrier section of the ATV and manufactures these at the firm\'s facility in\n       <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">\n        Turin\n       </a>\n       , Italy.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 31 July 2007, the first ATV,\n       <i>\n        Jules Verne\n       </i>\n       , arrived at the ESA spaceport in\n       <a href="/wiki/Kourou" title="Kourou">\n        Kourou\n       </a>\n       , French Guiana, after a nearly two week journey from\n       <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">\n        Rotterdam\n       </a>\n       harbour.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESA-shipping_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ESA-shipping-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 9 March 2008,\n       <i>\n        Jules Verne\n       </i>\n       was launched on top of an Ariane 5 rocket from Kourou.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 3 April 2008,\n       <i>\n        Jules Verne\n       </i>\n       succeeded in automatically docking with the ISS, proving the capabilities of the ESA\'s first fully automated, expendable cargo resupply spacecraft.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The arrival of the ATV came at a time at which there were public concerns over the logistical practicality of supplying the ISS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition to its use by ESA and Russia, the ATV was at one point under consider to perform services for NASA as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services" title="Commercial Orbital Transportation Services">\n        Commercial Orbital Transportation Services\n       </a>\n       program to replace the retiring\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       in its orbital cargo carrying capacity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2007_nasa_supply_26-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2007_nasa_supply-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Under the proposal, which had been issued by a joint venture between EADS and\n       <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">\n        Boeing\n       </a>\n       , the ATV would be launched from\n       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Canaveral" title="Cape Canaveral">\n        Cape Canaveral\n       </a>\n       , Florida, using a\n       <a href="/wiki/Delta_IV" title="Delta IV">\n        Delta IV\n       </a>\n       rocket.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One speculated use for NASA\'s ATV was to achieve the de-orbiting of the ISS once the space station had reached the end of its service life, being the only vehicle capable of doing so at that time after the Shuttle\'s retirement.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ultimately, the proposal was not awarded with a corresponding contract.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Design">\n        Design\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Design">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <i>\n        Automated Transfer Vehicle\n       </i>\n       (ATV) was an expendable\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automated_cargo_spacecraft" title="Automated cargo spacecraft">\n        cargo spacecraft\n       </a>\n       . Each vehicle consisted of two distinct sections, the systems bus and the integrated cargo carrier.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The system bus contained the ATV\'s propulsion system, avionics bays, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Solar_cell" title="Solar cell">\n        solar arrays\n       </a>\n       ; it was principally used following the vehicle\'s detachment from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">\n        Ariane 5\n       </a>\n       launcher to automatically traverse the remaining distance and dock with the ISS, the system bus would be inaccessible to the astronauts on board.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The integrated cargo carrier consisted of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Cabin_pressurization" title="Cabin pressurization">\n        pressurised\n       </a>\n       module, external bays for fluid and gas cargoes, further avionics and rendezvous sensors, and the docking mechanism. The primary structure of the ATV is protected by a\n       <a href="/wiki/Whipple_shield" title="Whipple shield">\n        meteorite and debris protection system\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The docking system of the ATV consists of a pair of\n       <a href="/wiki/Videometer" title="Videometer">\n        videometers\n       </a>\n       and a pair of\n       <a href="/wiki/Telegoniometer" title="Telegoniometer">\n        telegoniometers\n       </a>\n       manufactured by Sodern, a subsidiary of\n       <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">\n        Airbus\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Data processing for the rendezvous docking maneuver and emergency abort systems were designed and manufactured by\n       <a href="/wiki/CRISA" title="CRISA">\n        CRISA\n       </a>\n       . Additional monitoring data and redundancy was provided by the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurs_(docking_system)" title="Kurs (docking system)">\n        Kurs\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       automatic docking system, which was also used by Soyuz and Progress spacecraft. Visual imagery is provided by a camera on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Zvezda_(ISS_module)" title="Zvezda (ISS module)">\n        Zvezda ISS module\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In terms of its role, the ATV was designed to complement the smaller Russian\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progress_spacecraft" title="Progress spacecraft">\n        Progress spacecraft\n       </a>\n       , possessing three times its useful payload capacity. Similar to the Progress, it would carry both\n       <a href="/wiki/Bulk_cargo" title="Bulk cargo">\n        bulk liquids\n       </a>\n       and relatively fragile freight, which would be stored within a cargo hold maintained at a pressurized\n       <a href="/wiki/Shirt-sleeve_environment" title="Shirt-sleeve environment">\n        shirt-sleeve environment\n       </a>\n       in order that astronauts would be able to access payloads without the need to put on spacesuits. The pressurized cargo section of the ATV was based on the Italian-built\n       <a href="/wiki/Multi-Purpose_Logistics_Module" title="Multi-Purpose Logistics Module">\n        Multi-Purpose Logistics Module\n       </a>\n       (MPLM), which was a\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Shuttle\n       </a>\n       -carried "space barge" that had been previously used for transporting equipment to and from the Station. Unlike the MPLM, the ATV used the same docking mechanism as employed upon the Progress.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The ATV, like the Progress, also serves as a container for the station\'s waste. Each ATV weighs 20.7 tonnes at launch and has a cargo capacity of 8 tonnes:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esaspecs_3-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-esaspecs-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        1,500 kilograms (3,300\xc2\xa0lb) to 5,500 kilograms (12,100\xc2\xa0lb) of dry cargo (re-supply goods, scientific payload, etc.),\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Up to 840 kilograms (1,850\xc2\xa0lb) of water,\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Up to 100 kilograms (220\xc2\xa0lb) of gas (nitrogen, oxygen, air), with up to two gases per flight,\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Up to 4,700 kilograms (10,400\xc2\xa0lb) of propellant for the\n        <i>\n         re-boost\n        </i>\n        maneuver and refueling the station. The ATV propellant used for\n        <i>\n         re-boost\n        </i>\n        (\n        <a href="/wiki/Monomethylhydrazine" title="Monomethylhydrazine">\n         monomethylhydrazine\n        </a>\n        fuel and\n        <a href="/wiki/Dinitrogen_tetroxide" title="Dinitrogen tetroxide">\n         N\n         <sub>\n          2\n         </sub>\n         O\n         <sub>\n          4\n         </sub>\n        </a>\n        <a href="/wiki/Oxidizing_agent" title="Oxidizing agent">\n         oxidizer\n        </a>\n        ) is of a different type from the\n        <i>\n         payload\n        </i>\n        refueling propellant (\n        <a href="/wiki/Unsymmetrical_dimethylhydrazine" title="Unsymmetrical dimethylhydrazine">\n         UDMH\n        </a>\n        fuel and\n        <a href="/wiki/Dinitrogen_tetroxide" title="Dinitrogen tetroxide">\n         N\n         <sub>\n          2\n         </sub>\n         O\n         <sub>\n          4\n         </sub>\n        </a>\n        oxidizer).\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Use">\n        Use\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Use">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS_after_STS-124_06_2008.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2033" data-file-width="3061" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/ISS_after_STS-124_06_2008.jpg/220px-ISS_after_STS-124_06_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/ISS_after_STS-124_06_2008.jpg/330px-ISS_after_STS-124_06_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/ISS_after_STS-124_06_2008.jpg/440px-ISS_after_STS-124_06_2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ISS_after_STS-124_06_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Jules Verne\n         </i>\n         seen at the bottom of the ISS making the relative size clearly visible\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       ATVs were intended to be routinely launched every 17 months to conduct resupply missions to the International Space Station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The vehicle was launched into an orbital plane compatible with the ISS via the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">\n        Ariane 5\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Expendable_launch_system" title="Expendable launch system">\n        expendable launch system\n       </a>\n       ; shortly after detaching from the launcher, the ATV would deploy its solar panels.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Over an average mission time of 100 hours, it would perform phasing manoeuvers from its initial orbital high point under direct control from the ground-based\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Operations_Centre" title="European Space Operations Centre">\n        European Space Operations Centre\n       </a>\n       at\n       <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt" title="Darmstadt">\n        Darmstadt\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">\n        Germany\n       </a>\n       using NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Tracking_and_Data_Relay_Satellite_System" title="Tracking and Data Relay Satellite System">\n        Tracking and Data Relay Satellite System\n       </a>\n       . A second series of manoeuvres would bring the ATV to the precise altitude of the ISS before commencing integrated operations for the final approach with the Space Station, during which mission authority transferred to NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft_Jr._Mission_Control_Center" title="Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center">\n        Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">\n        Houston\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">\n        Texas\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The ATV would employ a combination of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPS" title="GPS">\n        GPS\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Celestial_navigation" title="Celestial navigation">\n        astronavigation\n       </a>\n       techniques to automatically rendezvous with the Space Station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Telemetry" title="Telemetry">\n        Telemetry\n       </a>\n       contact was established between the ISS and ATV during its preparations for the final approach. Once at a distance of 249 m, the onboard computers of the ATV employed both videometer and telegoniometer data to perform the final approach and docking manoeuvres; the docking itself to the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Zvezda_(ISS_module)" title="Zvezda (ISS module)">\n         Zvezda\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       module, was fully automated. In the event of are any last-minute technical issues or problems, a pre-programmed sequence of anti-collision manoeuvres, fully independent of the main navigation system, can be activated by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Astronautics" title="Astronautics">\n        flight engineers\n       </a>\n       aboard the station. Upon contact with the module, the automatic capture sequence would be activated.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Once the ATV had successfully docked, the station crew would be able to enter the vehicle\'s cargo section and directly access the payload on board.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The ATV\'s liquid tanks would be connected to the station\'s plumbing by the crew to discharge their contents in a controlled manner, while the station crew would manually release air components directly into the ISS\'s atmosphere. For up to six months, the ATV, which would remain mainly in dormant mode, could remain attached to the ISS with the hatch remaining open throughout.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The crew would then steadily fill the cargo section with the station\'s waste material for disposal. At intervals of 10 to 45 days, the ATV would be reactivated and its thrusters would typically be used to boost the station\'s altitude.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Once its mission was accomplished, the ATV, which would often be filled with up to 6.5 tonnes of waste, would separate from the ISS. Its thrusters would deliberately move the spacecraft out of orbit (de-orbit) and place it on a steep flight path to perform a controlled destructive\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Re-entry" title="Re-entry">\n        re-entry\n       </a>\n       high above the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">\n        Pacific Ocean\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atv_biway_14-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-atv_biway-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182.66666666667px">\n        <div style="width: 182.66666666667px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 180.66666666667px;">\n          <div style="margin:0px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ATV-2_launch_from_ISS.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/ATV-2_launch_from_ISS.jpg/271px-ATV-2_launch_from_ISS.jpg" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/ATV-2_launch_from_ISS.jpg/541px-ATV-2_launch_from_ISS.jpg 2x" width="181"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           <i>\n            Johannes Kepler\n           </i>\n           Automated Transfer Vehicle\'s launch as seen from the ISS\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182.66666666667px">\n        <div style="width: 182.66666666667px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width:         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           ATV interior with\n           <a href="/wiki/Expedition_17" title="Expedition 17">\n            Expedition 17\n re-enters Earth\'s atmosphere in a controlled burn-up after undocking from ISS\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Designation\n        </th>\n        <th>\n <td>\n         28 March 2012\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         4 October 2012\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n          <a href="#cite_note-48">\n           [48]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n          <a href="#cite_note-49">\n           [49]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup href="#cite_note-SpaceTravel-51">\n           [51]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         ATV-4\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein_ATV" title="Albert Einstein ATV">\n           Albert Einstein\n          </a>\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         5 June 2013\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         15 June 2013\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2 November 2013\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n          <a href="#cite_note-52">\n           [52]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n          <a href="#cite_note-53">\n           [53]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n          <a href="#cite_note-54">\n           [54]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n 2014\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         12 August 2014\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         15 February 2015\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n
