</a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="6" style="text-align: center;">\n         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar">\n          <ul>\n           <li class="nv-view">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template:ATV_missions" title="Template:ATV missions">\n             <span title="View this template">\n              view\n             </span>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-talk">\n            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:ATV_missions" title="Template talk:ATV missions">\n             <span title="Discuss this template">\n              talk\n             </span>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n           <li class="nv-edit">\n            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:ATV_missions&amp;action=edit">\n             <span title="Edit this template">\n              edit\n             </span>\n            </a>\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       On 2 April 2012, the ESA announced that the ATV program would end after the fifth ATV had been launched in 2014. No additional ATVs will be funded.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spaceflightnow_6-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-spaceflightnow-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Jules_Verne">\n        Jules Verne\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Jules Verne">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Jules_Verne_ATV" title="Jules Verne ATV">\n        Jules Verne ATV\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jules_verne_at_iss.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1872" data-file-width="2848" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Jules_verne_at_iss.jpg/220px-Jules_verne_at_iss.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Jules_verne_at_iss.jpg/330px-Jules_verne_at_iss.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Jules_verne_at_iss.jpg/440px-Jules_verne_at_iss.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jules_verne_at_iss.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Jules Verne ATV at ISS, 2008\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The first flight of the ATV was delayed on multiple occasions prior to its launch on 9 March 2008. It was named\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Jules_Verne" title="Jules Verne">\n         Jules Verne\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , in memory of the first science fiction writer of modern times. The Jules Verne carried two of the author\'s original handwritten manuscripts, to be received by the ISS crew as symbolic tokens of the success of the first flight.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The craft was launched into a 300-kilometre (190\xc2\xa0mi)\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">\n        orbit\n       </a>\n       atop an Ariane 5 rocket from the equatorial\n       <a href="/wiki/ELA-3" title="ELA-3">\n        ELA-3\n       </a>\n       launch site at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Space_Centre" title="Guiana Space Centre">\n        Guiana Space Centre\n       </a>\n       . The ATV separated from the rocket and, following weeks of tests and orbit adjustments, successfully docked in the International Space Station at 14:45 UTC on 3 April 2008.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the early morning hours of 29 September 2008, the Jules Verne burnt up on entering the atmosphere above an uninhabited section of the Pacific Ocean, southwest of Tahiti.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Johannes_Kepler">\n        Johannes Kepler\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Johannes Kepler">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler_ATV" title="Johannes Kepler ATV">\n        Johannes Kepler ATV\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Launched on 17 February 2011,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Johannes Kepler was at the time the heaviest payload ever launched by the European Space Agency\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and carried 7000\xc2\xa0kg of cargo to the ISS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The first launch attempt on 15 February 2011 had been halted during the final countdown at four minutes from lift off due to an erroneous signal from one of the rocket\'s fuel tanks.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 29 April 2011, the engines of the ATV were used to rotate the ISS in order for a Russian\n       <a href="/wiki/Progress_(spacecraft)" title="Progress (spacecraft)">\n        Progress\n       </a>\n       supply craft to dock with the station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Due to the delayed launch of\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-134" title="STS-134">\n        STS-134\n       </a>\n       the mission of Johannes Kepler was extended, and it undocked from the ISS on 20 June 2011. It deorbited a day later on 21 June 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Edoardo_Amaldi">\n        Edoardo Amaldi\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Edoardo Amaldi">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Edoardo_Amaldi_ATV" title="Edoardo Amaldi ATV">\n        Edoardo Amaldi ATV\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ATV-3_approaches_the_International_Space_Station_7.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/ATV-3_approaches_the_International_Space_Station_7.jpg/220px-ATV-3_approaches_the_International_Space_Station_7.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/ATV-3_approaches_the_International_Space_Station_7.jpg/330px-ATV-3_approaches_the_International_Space_Station_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/ATV-3_approaches_the_International_Space_Station_7.jpg/440px-ATV-3_approaches_the_International_Space_Station_7.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ATV-3_approaches_the_International_Space_Station_7.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         ATV-3\n         <i>\n          Edoardo Amaldi\n         </i>\n         approaches ISS on the dark side of the Earth, 2012\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The third ATV vehicle arrived in French Guiana in late August 2011 and was launched on 23 March 2012.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It docked with the International Space Station at 2231 GMT on 28 March 2012.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Albert_Einstein">\n        Albert Einstein\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Albert Einstein">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein_ATV" title="Albert Einstein ATV">\n        Albert Einstein ATV\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Albert Einstein ATV was the heaviest spacecraft launched by Ariane at the time and lifted off at 21:52:11 GMT on 5 June 2013.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-launched_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-launched-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It docked with the ISS on 15 June 2013 at 14:07 GMT.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n        <a href="#cite_note-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="Georges_Lema\xc3\xaetre">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Georges_Lema.C3.AEtre">\n        Georges Lema\xc3\xaetre\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Georges Lema\xc3\xaetre">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Georges_Lema%C3%AEtre_ATV" title="Georges Lema\xc3\xaetre ATV">\n        Georges Lema\xc3\xaetre ATV\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Named after the Belgian astronomer\n       <a href="/wiki/Georges_Lema%C3%AEtre" title="Georges Lema\xc3\xaetre">\n        Georges Lema\xc3\xaetre\n       </a>\n       . The spacecraft launched during the night of 29 July (23:44 GMT, 20:44 local time, 30 July 01:44 CEST), 2014, on a mission to supply the International Space Station (ISS) with propellant, water, air, and dry cargo, and an artwork by artist\n       <a href="/wiki/Katie_Paterson" title="Katie Paterson">\n        Katie Paterson\n       </a>\n       . It docked with the ISS on 12 August at 13:30 GMT.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Georges Lema\xc3\xaetre had a total mass of almost 20.3 tonnes, a mass that exceeded that of all previously launched ATVs. This also made it the heaviest spacecraft ever launched by an Ariane rocket.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="ATV_Control_Centre">\n        ATV Control Centre\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: ATV Control Centre">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       ATV missions were monitored and controlled from the ATV Control Centre (ATV-CC), located at the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toulouse_Space_Centre" title="Toulouse Space Centre">\n        Toulouse Space Centre\n       </a>\n       (CST) in\n       <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">\n        Toulouse\n       </a>\n       , France. The ATV-CC was responsible for the planning and the issuing of commands for the orbital maneuvers and mission tasks of each ATV, from the moment of separation from its launch vehicle, until it burns up in the Earth\'s atmosphere. The ATV-CC has a direct communication line with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbus_Control_Center" title="Columbus Control Center">\n        Columbus Control Center\n       </a>\n       (Col-CC) in\n       <a href="/wiki/Oberpfaffenhofen" title="Oberpfaffenhofen">\n        Oberpfaffenhofen\n       </a>\n       , Germany. Col-CC provides ATV-CC with access to both the NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Tracking_and_Data_Relay_Satellite_System" title="Tracking and Data Relay Satellite System">\n        Tracking and Data Relay Satellite System\n       </a>\n       and the European\n       <a href="/wiki/Artemis_(satellite)" title="Artemis (satellite)">\n        Artemis\n       </a>\n       communication networks in order to communicate with both the ATV and the ISS. The ATV-CC coordinated its actions with NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft_Jr._Mission_Control_Center" title="Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center">\n        Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center\n       </a>\n       (MCC-H) in\n       <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">\n        Houston\n       </a>\n       and the Russian\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=FKA_Mission_Control_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="FKA Mission Control Center (page does not exist)">\n        FKA Mission Control Center\n       </a>\n       (TsUP or MCC-M) in\n       <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">\n        Moscow\n       </a>\n       , as well as the ATV launch site at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Space_Centre" title="Guiana Space Centre">\n        Guiana Space Centre\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Kourou" title="Kourou">\n        Kourou\n       </a>\n       , French Guiana.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATV-CC_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ATV-CC-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Orion_Service_Module">\n        Orion Service Module\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Orion Service Module">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Orion_Service_Module" title="Orion Service Module">\n        Orion Service Module\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="4267" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg/220px-Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg/330px-Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg/440px-Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Orion_with_ATV_SM.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Orion spacecraft including the ATV derived Service Module\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In May 2011 the ESA director general announced a possible collaboration with NASA to work on a successor to the ATV.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Later that year, a proposal to utilise an ATV derived service module for NASA\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Orion_(spacecraft)" title="Orion (spacecraft)">\n        Orion\n       </a>\n       capsule was revealed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This service module would be provided as barter for the ESA\'s 8% share of the operating expense of the ISS, which had been fulfilled up to 2017 by the five ATVs. Developing a service module for Orion would cover the ESA\'s share of ISS operation up to 2020.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:23em; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">\n       <div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">\n        <div>\n         "ESA\xe2\x80\x99s contribution is going to be critical to the success of Orion\xe2\x80\x99s 2017 mission"\n        </div>\n       </div>\n       <cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">\n        \xe2\x80\x94NASA Orion Program manager\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-osm_10-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-osm-10">\n          [10]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </cite>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In June 2012, the ESA awarded two separate studies to Airbus, each worth \xe2\x82\xac6.5 million, to evaluate options for using technology and experience gained from ATV and\n       <a href="/wiki/Columbus_(ISS_module)" title="Columbus (ISS module)">\n        Columbus\n       </a>\n       related work to cover the ESA\'s share of ISS operation past 2017.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One study looked into developing a service module for Orion, while the other examined development of a multipurpose vehicle that could resupply space stations, remove debris, and service satellites in orbit. The studies were to be completed before the end of 2012\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At the meeting of the ESA Ministerial Council in November 2012, the ESA committed to developing the service module,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and in mid-December signed an agreement with NASA to provide an\n       <a href="/wiki/Orion_Service_Module" title="Orion Service Module">\n        ATV derived Orion Service Module\n       </a>\n       for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Exploration_Mission_1" title="Exploration Mission 1">\n        first launch\n       </a>\n       of Orion on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Launch_System" title="Space Launch System">\n        Space Launch System\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-osm_10-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-osm-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The ESA awarded\n       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Defence_and_Space" title="Airbus Defence and Space">\n        Airbus Defence and Space\n       </a>\n       a \xe2\x82\xac390 million ($488 million) contract in November 2014 to develop and build the module.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution_proposals">\n        Evolution proposals\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Evolution proposals">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In addition to its principal role as a one-way uncrewed cargo transfer vehicle, from the onset of work on the project, the ESA had viewed the ATV as having the potential for being the starting point for a whole family of automated space vehicles.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Amongst the conceived missions for ATV-derived vehicles have been orbital automated construction programmes and independent bases for experiments, as well as a potential upgraded version of the ATV that would survive reentry intact, enabling its use as a two-way cargo transfer vehicle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1998_deliv_12-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-1998_deliv-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atv_biway_14-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-atv_biway-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The potential commercialisation of the ATV was also the subject of a formal study conducted by the ESA, during which the prospects of using the spacecraft as a dedicated tug for reorbiting satellites, as well as the use of alternative launch systems, were examined.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following the decision by NASA to retire the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       in 2011, the ESA decided to launch a further series of studies to determine the potential for evolutions and adaptations of the ATV. As a result of these studies, the cargo return version (CARV) was identified as a particularly promising candidate for further development. The goal of this variant is to provide ESA with the capability to transport scientific data and cargo from the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        ISS\n       </a>\n       to Earth. Beyond this, CARV could be enhanced to become a crew vehicle which would be launched by an adapted\n       <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">\n        Ariane 5\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Mini Space Station\n       </dt>\n       <dd>\n        The MSS concept is an ATV evolution proposal for the construction of multiple ATVs with two docking ports, one at each end. The current version of the ATV is already prepared for a docking port at the back, with the main propulsion system arranged in a cylindrical fashion leaving room for a tunnel through the middle. This concept would allow\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_spacecraft" title="Soyuz spacecraft">\n         Soyuz\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progress_spacecraft" title="Progress spacecraft">\n         Progress\n        </a>\n        and other ATVs to dock to the back of the ATV, allowing a steady flow of Russian vehicles using the available docking ports whilst an ATV is docked for an average of around 6 months at a time.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATV_Evo_79-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ATV_Evo-79">\n          [79]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Payload Retrieval System\n       </dt>\n       <dd>\n        The PARES would have included a small ballistic capsule similar to\n        <a href="/wiki/VBK-Raduga" title="VBK-Raduga">\n         VBK-Raduga\n        </a>\n        embedded into the ATV docking interface, which would have brought back a few tens of kilograms of payload. PARES could have featured a deployable heat shield system. The\n        <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">\n         European Space Agency\n        </a>\n        was also proposing the system for use with the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progress_spacecraft" title="Progress spacecraft">\n         Progress spacecraft\n        </a>\n        and the\n        <a href="/wiki/H-II_Transfer_Vehicle" title="H-II Transfer Vehicle">\n         H-II Transfer Vehicle (HTV)\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATV_Evo_79-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ATV_Evo-79">\n          [79]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n         <a href="#cite_note-80">\n          [80]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Cargo Ascent and Return Vehicle\n       </dt>\n       <dd>\n        The CARV would deliver a redesigned capsule, capable of bringing back payload from orbit. It could be installed in place of the ATV pressurized cargo hold. In addition, it could be adapted to dock at the US side of the station. Given the larger docking ports there, it would be possible to transfer complete\n        <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Payload_Rack" title="International Standard Payload Rack">\n         International Standard Payload Racks\n        </a>\n        (ISPRs) from the ATV to the station, which is not currently possible.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATV_Evo_79-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ATV_Evo-79">\n          [79]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <dl>\n       <dt>\n        Crew Transport Vehicle\n       </dt>\n       <dd>\n        This is another option under consideration. Similar to the CARV variant, this would replace the current\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Integrated_Cargo_Carrier" title="Integrated Cargo Carrier">\n         Integrated Cargo Carrier\n        </a>\n        with a pressurized re-entry capsule. A significant difference with the cargo-only variant would be the presence of a Crew Escape System, consisting of a number of booster rockets able to pull the crew capsule away from the launcher (Ariane 5) and/or Service Module in the event of an emergency. The CTV variant of the ATV could be able to seat 4 or 5 crew members.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATV_Evo_79-3">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ATV_Evo-79">\n          [79]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Possibilities for launching of the ATV on other launchers than the Ariane 5 have also been investigated, in particular in the frame of\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services" title="Commercial Orbital Transportation Services">\n        Commercial Orbital Transportation Services\n       </a>\n       . ESA and its member states will consider approval for further ATV development in the coming years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATV_Evo_79-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ATV_Evo-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">\n        <div style="width: 162px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">\n          <div style="margin:0px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cargo_Ascent_and_Return_Vehicle_docked_to_the_ISS.jpg">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="400" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ce/Cargo_Ascent_and_Return_Vehicle_docked_to_the_ISS.jpg/240px-Cargo_Ascent_and_Return_Vehicle_docked_to_the_ISS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/ce/Cargo_Ascent_and_Return_Vehicle_docked_to_the_ISS.jpg/360px-Cargo_Ascent_and_Return_Vehicle_docked_to_the_ISS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/ce/Cargo_Ascent_and_Return_Vehicle_docked_to_the_ISS.jpg 2x" width="160"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           An MSS could be used as a small orbital lab\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 159.33333333333px">\n        <div style="width: 159.33333333333px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 157.33333333333px;">\n          <div style="margin:0px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ATV_PARES.JPG">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="333" data-file-width="436" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/ATV_PARES.JPG/236px-ATV_PARES.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e0/ATV_PARES.JPG/354px-ATV_PARES.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/e0/ATV_PARES.JPG 2x" width="158"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           PARES capsules would be able to hold a few kg of cargo\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 152.66666666667px">\n        <div style="width: 152.66666666667px">\n         <div class="thumb" style="width: 150.66666666667px;">\n          <div style="margin:0px auto;">\n           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ATV_CARV.JPG">\n            <img alt="" data-file-height="319" data-file-width="400" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9c/ATV_CARV.JPG/226px-ATV_CARV.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9c/ATV_CARV.JPG/339px-ATV_CARV.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/9c/ATV_CARV.JPG 2x" width="151"/>\n           </a>\n          </div>\n         </div>\n         <div class="gallerytext">\n          <p>\n           CARV would be used to transport a large amount of cargo to Earth\n          </p>\n         </div>\n        </div>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_crewed_version">\n        Proposed crewed version\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Proposed crewed version">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Automated_Transfer_Vehicle_capsule_-_3D_render.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="196" data-file-width="250" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3a/Automated_Transfer_Vehicle_capsule_-_3D_render.jpg/220px-Automated_Transfer_Vehicle_capsule_-_3D_render.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/3a/Automated_Transfer_Vehicle_capsule_-_3D_render.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Automated_Transfer_Vehicle_capsule_-_3D_render.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A 3D rendering of the proposed ATV derived crewed transportation system.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Both the ESA and the manufacturing team have considered various programmes under which the ATV, or portions of the technologies composing it, would have been developed into a crewed configuration.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 14 May 2008, aerospace company\n       <a href="/wiki/Airbus_Defence_and_Space" title="Airbus Defence and Space">\n        EADS Astrium\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/German_Aerospace_Center" title="German Aerospace Center">\n        German Aerospace Center\n       </a>\n       (DLR), announced that they were actively pursuing a development project with the aim of adapting the ATV into a crew transportation system.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the envisioned configuration, the craft would be able to launch a 3-person crew beyond\n       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n        LEO\n       </a>\n       via use of a modified version of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">\n        Ariane 5\n       </a>\n       rocket and would be more spacious than the Russian Soyuz. A mock-up of the proposed craft was publicly displayed at the 2008\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internationale_Luft-_und_Raumfahrtausstellung" title="Internationale Luft- und Raumfahrtausstellung">\n        International Aerospace Exhibition\n       </a>\n       in Berlin.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_83-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       If the project were to have been given ESA approval, development would have proceeded in two stages:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The first stage would have involved the development of an Advanced Reentry Vehicle (ARV)\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa2_85-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-esa2-85">\n          [85]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        capable of transporting up to 1,500\xc2\xa0kg of cargo from space to earth safely (see\n        <i>\n         CARV\n        </i>\n        above) by 2015.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-esa1_86-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-esa1-86">\n          [86]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        This capability would be available to ESA even if further development were to be halted. It would prove useful in the ISS program as well as the proposed\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_Sample_Return_Mission" title="Mars Sample Return Mission">\n         Mars Sample Return Mission\n        </a>\n        with NASA. ARV development would make use of work done on the\n        <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_Reentry_Demonstrator" title="Atmospheric Reentry Demonstrator">\n         Atmospheric Reentry Demonstrator\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Crew_Return_Vehicle" title="Crew Return Vehicle">\n         Crew Return Vehicle\n        </a>\n        and related projects. The budget for this stage of the ATV overhaul would reportedly be \xe2\x82\xac300\xc2\xa0million.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n         <a href="#cite_note-87">\n          [87]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">\n         <a href="#cite_note-88">\n          [88]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flightglobal1_89-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-flightglobal1-89">\n          [89]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The second stage would adapt the then existing capsule to be able to transport people safely as well as upgrade the propulsion and other systems in the service module and would last 4 to 5 years at a cost of "a couple of billion [euro]" according to a senior Astrium representative.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_83-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-83">\n          [83]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n         <a href="#cite_note-90">\n          [90]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n         <a href="#cite_note-91">\n          [91]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       In November 2008, ESA ministers budgeted for a feasibility study into developing a re-entry capsule for the ATV, a requirement for developing either a cargo return capacity or a crew version of the ATV.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 7 July 2009, the ESA signed a \xe2\x82\xac21\xc2\xa0million study contract with EADS Astrium.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The ARV effort was ultimately discontinued after completing the B1 stage due to fiscal constraints resulting from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late-2000s_financial_crisis" title="Late-2000s financial crisis">\n        Late-2000s financial crisis\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Exoliner">\n        Exoliner\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Exoliner">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       During the 2010s, Lockheed Martin put together a proposal for\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Resupply_Services#Commercial_Resupply_Services_2" title="Commercial Resupply Services">\n        Commercial Resupply Services 2\n       </a>\n       that included a new 4.4-meter (14\xc2\xa0ft) diameter cargo transport module called\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exoliner" title="Exoliner">\n         Exoliner\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , which was based on the ATV and was to be jointly developed with\n       <a href="/wiki/Thales_Alenia_Space" title="Thales Alenia Space">\n        Thales Alenia Space\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpaceNews-2015-03-13_96-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SpaceNews-2015-03-13-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dbj20150312_97-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dbj20150312-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Automated_Transfer_Vehicle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_space_station_cargo_vehicles" title="Comparison of space station cargo vehicles">\n         Comparison of space station cargo vehicles\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services" title="Commercial Orbital Transportation Services">\n         Commercial Orbital Transportation Services\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 NASA initiative to create a commercial cargo and crew transportation capability to and from the ISS.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/CSTS" title="CSTS">\n         CSTS\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automated_cargo_spacecraft" title="Automated cargo spacecraft">\n         Automated cargo spacecraft\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x93 other ISS resupply vehicles:\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cygnus_spacecraft" title="Cygnus spacecraft">\n           Cygnus spacecraft\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 developed by\n          <a href="/wiki/Orbital_Sciences_Corporation" title="Orbital Sciences Corporation">\n           Orbital Sciences Corporation\n          </a>\n          .\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_Dragon" title="SpaceX Dragon">\n           Dragon Cargo spacecraft\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 vehicle capable of returning cargo to Earth,\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sx20090918_99-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-sx20090918-99">\n            [99]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          developed by\n          <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n           SpaceX\n          </a>\n          .\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/H-II_Transfer_Vehicle" title="H-II Transfer Vehicle">\n           H-II Transfer Vehicle\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 developed by\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japan_Aerospace_Exploration_Agency" title="Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency">\n           Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency\n          </a>\n          .\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Progress_(spacecraft)" title="Progress (spacecraft)">\n           Progress spacecraft\n          </a>\n          \xe2\x80\x93 developed by\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federal_Space_Agency" title="Russian Federal Space Agency">\n           Russian Federal Space Agency\n          </a>\n          .\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Excalibur_Almaz" title="Excalibur Almaz">\n         Excalibur Almaz\n        </a>\n        , which plans for their capsule to use a service module based on the ATV design, according to Art Dula, the chairman of Excalibur Almaz.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mbEA2_100-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-mbEA2-100">\n          [100]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/European_contribution_to_the_International_Space_Station" title="European contribution to the International Space Station">\n         European contribution to the International Space Station\n        </a>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n        References\n       </span>\n
